24:T858d,<entryFree id="n14139" key="ذُو" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ذُو</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> meaning <foreign lang="ar">صَاحِب</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">A possessor, an owner, a lord,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a master,</hi> but often better rendered <hi rend="ital">having, possessing, possessed of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">endowed with</hi>], (T, S, M, Mgh, Msb, K, but omitted in the CK,) used as a prefixed noun, (S, Mgh, Msb, &amp;c.,) is originally <foreign lang="ar">ذَوًا</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">عَصًا</foreign>, the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> being changed from <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>; (S;) or it is originally <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَّى</foreign>; and if one used it as a proper name, he would say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا ذَوَّىقَدْ جَآءَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is Dhawà, he has come</hi>]; (M;) [not <foreign lang="ar">ذَوًا</foreign>, as in copies of the S; i. e.,] its third radical letter is <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>, not, as J says, <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>; this <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> being afterwards suppressed; (IB;) [so that the word becomes <foreign lang="ar">ذَوٌ</foreign>, and then, by reason of its being prefixed to another noun, <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">أَبَوٌ</foreign>, the original form of <foreign lang="ar">أَبٌ</foreign>, becomes <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو</foreign>:] it is declined [like <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو</foreign>] with <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> and | and <foreign lang="ar">ىِ</foreign>; (Msb;) [i. e.,] the nom. case is <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign>, accus. <foreign lang="ar">ذَا</foreign>, and gen. <foreign lang="ar">ذِى</foreign>: (Mgh:) the fem. is <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتُ</foreign>; (T, S, M, Mgh, Msb, K; in a copy of the M, <foreign lang="ar">ذاة</foreign>, and the CK, <foreign lang="ar">ذَاةٌ</foreign> [as though it were not a prefixed noun];) and in the case of a pause, some say <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتْ</foreign>, and others say <foreign lang="ar">ذَاهْ</foreign>: (Lth, T: the latter usage, only, is mentioned in the S:) dual. masc., <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَا</foreign>, (S, * M,) [accus and gen. <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَىْ</foreign>;] fem. <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتَا</foreign>, (T, M, Mgh, Msb, K,) for which <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتَا</foreign> is allowable in poetry, but <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتَا</foreign> is better, (T,) [accus, and gen. <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتَىْ</foreign>:] pl., masc., <foreign lang="ar">ذَوُو</foreign>, (T, *, S, * M, Msb, K, but omitted in the CK,) [accus, and gen. <foreign lang="ar">ذَوِى</foreign>;] fem. <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتُ</foreign>, (T, S, * M, Mgh, Msb, K,) accus. and gen. <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتِ</foreign>; (S;) and <foreign lang="ar">أُولُو</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أُولَات</foreign> are like <foreign lang="ar">ذَوُو</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَات</foreign> [in signification]. (T. [See art. <foreign lang="ar">الو</foreign>.]) In this sense it is not used otherwise than as a prefixed noun: when used to characterize an indeterminate noun, prefixed to an indeterminate noun; and when used to characterize a determinate noun, prefixed to [a noun rendered determinate by] the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>. (S.) [Thus you say <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ ذُو مَالٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A man a possessor of wealth;</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">الرَّجُلُ ذُو المَالِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The man the possessor of wealth</hi>.] In the phrase <foreign lang="ar">غَيْرَ ذَاتِ الشَوْكَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Not those possessed of weapons,</hi> &amp;c.], in the Kur [viii. 7], the fem. form is used as meaning the <foreign lang="ar">طَائِفَة</foreign> [or party]. (T.) <foreign lang="ar">صَارَ ذَا ذَنْبٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He became one having a sin,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">crime,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">attributable to him,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">he had a sin,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">attributable to him,</hi>] means <foreign lang="ar">تَحَمَّلَ ذَنْبًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he became chargeable with a sin,</hi> &amp;c.]. (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">ذنب</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Accord. to the S, it is not prefixed to a pronoun (<foreign lang="ar">مُضْمَر</foreign>); nor to a proper name, such as <foreign lang="ar">زَيْد</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَمْرو</foreign> and the like: but there are several instances of its being prefixed, in its pl. form, to a pronoun; among which is the saying of a poet, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّمَا يَصْطَنِعُ المَعْرُوفُ فِى النَّاسِ ذَوُوهُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Only they who are possessors thereof do that which is good among men</hi>]: (TA:) [this usage, however, is perhaps only allowable by poetic license: see another ex. (also here cited in the TA) in the Ham p. 442, and the remarks there appended to it:] and it is also prefixed to proper names, as is shown by the phrase, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا ذُو</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٍ</foreign> (M, K, TA,) mentioned, as heard from the Arabs, by Ahmad Ibn-Ibráheem, the preceptor of Th, meaning <hi rend="ital">This is Zeyd,</hi> (M, TA,) i. e., <hi rend="ital">this is the owner of the name Zeyd;</hi> (M, K, TA;) and [perhaps] by the name <foreign lang="ar">ذُو الخَلَصَةِ</foreign>, for <foreign lang="ar">الخلصة</foreign> is [said by some to be] the name of a certain idol, and <foreign lang="ar">ذو</foreign> is a metonymical appellation of its <foreign lang="ar">بَيْت</foreign>; and by the proper names <foreign lang="ar">ذُو رُعَيْنٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذُو يَزَنَ</foreign> and [accord. to some] <foreign lang="ar">ذُو جَدْنٍ</foreign> [and the like, of which several are mentioned in the S, as well as in the M &amp;c.]. (IB, TA.) [But see a later portion of this paragraph, where, prefixed to a proper name, it is said to be redundant.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ذَوُو الأَرْحَام</foreign>, [or, as in the Kur viii. last verse, and xxxiii. 6, <foreign lang="ar">أُولُو الأَرْحَامِ</foreign>, pls. of <foreign lang="ar">ذُو الرَّحِمِ</foreign>,] in the classical <pb n="985"/> language, means [<hi rend="ital">The possessors of relationship;</hi> i. e.] any <hi rend="ital">relations:</hi> and in law, any <hi rend="ital">relations that have no portion</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of the inheritances termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَرَائِض</foreign>] <hi rend="ital">and are not</hi> [<hi rend="ital">such heirs as are designated by the appellation</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">عَصَبَة</foreign> [q. v.: they are so called because they are <hi rend="ital">relations by the women's side:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">رَحِمٌ</foreign>]. (KT, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  If you form a pl. from <foreign lang="ar">ذُومَالٍ</foreign>, you say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰؤُلَآءِ ذَوُونَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">These are possessors</hi> of wealth]; because in this case the pl. is not a prefixed noun. (S.) Accord. to Lth, <foreign lang="ar">الذَّوُونَ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">The former,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">first,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of persons,</hi>] and <hi rend="ital">the more,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">most, distinguished.</hi> (T, TA. *) Also, (S, M,) and <foreign lang="ar">الأَذْوَآءُ</foreign>, [which is another pl. of <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign>,] (S,) <hi rend="ital">The kings</hi> (S, M) <hi rend="ital">of El-Yemen, of the tribe of Kudá'ah,</hi> (S,) <hi rend="ital">whose surnames commenced with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign>, (M,) [i. e.] <hi rend="ital">who were named</hi> [or rather <hi rend="ital">surnamed</hi>] (S) <foreign lang="ar">ذُو يَزَنَ</foreign> (S, M) <hi rend="ital">and</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذُو جَدَنٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">and</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ذُو نُوَاسٍ</foreign> (S) <hi rend="ital">and the like.</hi> (S, M.) <foreign lang="ar">قُرَشِىٌّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ مِنْ ذِى وَلَا ذُو</foreign>, occurring in a trad., means <hi rend="ital">A Kurashee</hi> in respect of lineage, <hi rend="ital">not of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَذْوَآء</foreign> [above mentioned]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذَات</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذِى</foreign> are also used as prefixed nouns in various expressions here following, in several thereof as meaning <hi rend="ital">Something in possession,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like; not a possessor:</hi> or, in these instances, as is said in explanation of the first of the following phrases, and also of the phrase <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتُ اليَدِ</foreign> (mentioned below) in Har p. 93, that which is contained is made to be as though it were the possessor (<foreign lang="ar">صَاحِب</foreign>) of that which contains.]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَوَّتَ ذَابَطْنِهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He killed what was in her belly</hi>]. (Har ubi suprá.) And <foreign lang="ar">وَضَعَتِ المَرْأَةُ ذَا بَطْنِهَا</foreign>, (T,) or <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتَ</foreign>

(M.)          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتٌ</foreign> is sometimes used as a noun independent in its meaning, (Mgh, Msb,) so as to denote material [or real] things; (Msb;) and is described by the epithets <foreign lang="ar">مُتَمَيِّزَةٌ</foreign> [or “ distinct ”] (Mgh, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">قَدِيمَةٌ</foreign> [as meaning “ that has existed from eternity ”] (Mgh) and <foreign lang="ar">مُحْدَثَةٌ</foreign> [as meaning “ that has been brought into existence ”]. (Mgh, Msb.) Thus used, (Msb,) it signifies The <hi rend="ital">essence</hi> of a thing, meaning <hi rend="ital">that by being which a thing is what it is,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">that in being which a thing consists;</hi> or the <hi rend="ital">ultimate and radical constituent</hi> of a thing: and the <hi rend="ital">essence</hi> as meaning the <hi rend="ital">peculiar nature</hi> of a thing: syn. <foreign lang="ar">حَقِيقَةٌ</foreign>, (T, IB, Msb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَاهِيَّةٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">خَاصَّةٌ</foreign>: (T, IB, TA:) it is also used as meaning a thing's <hi rend="ital">self:</hi> (Mgh, * Msb:) [a man's <hi rend="ital">self,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">person:</hi> (see <foreign lang="ar">شَخْصٌ</foreign>:)] and <hi rend="ital">a thing; a being; anything, whatever it be;</hi> every <foreign lang="ar">شَىْء</foreign> being a <foreign lang="ar">ذَات</foreign>, and every <foreign lang="ar">ذات</foreign> being a <foreign lang="ar">شىء</foreign>: (Aboo-Sa'eed, Mgh, Msb:) and particularly <hi rend="ital">a substance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thing that subsists by itself:</hi> [hence <foreign lang="ar">اِسْمُ ذَاتٍ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">a real substantive;</hi> also termed <foreign lang="ar">اِسْمُ عَيْنٍ</foreign>: opposed to <foreign lang="ar">اِسْمُ مَعْنًى</foreign>, i. e. an ideal substantive:] and [hence] it signifies also <hi rend="ital">a word that is independent in its meaning;</hi> [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتٌ</foreign> (alone), though oftener used in the sense assigned above to <foreign lang="ar">اِسْمُ ذَاتٍ</foreign>, signifies also, absolutely, <hi rend="ital">a substantive;</hi>] opposed to <foreign lang="ar">صِفَةٌ</foreign> as signifying a word that is not independent in its meaning. (Kull p. 187.) Its application to God, in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">حَقِيقَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">خَاصَّةٌ</foreign>, is forbidden by most persons: (TA:) [for] <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [as meaning <hi rend="ital">The essence of God</hi>], used by the scholastic theologians, is said to be an ignorant expression, because the names of God do not admit the fem. affix <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>; so that one does not apply to Him the epithet <foreign lang="ar">عَلَّامَةٌ</foreign>, though He is the all-surpassing in knowledge. (Msb.) The phrase <foreign lang="ar">فِى ذَاتِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> is like <foreign lang="ar">فِى جَنْبِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">In,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in respect of, that which is the right,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">due, of God;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in respect of, obedience to God,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the means of obtaining nearness to God,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the way of God</hi>]: and like <foreign lang="ar">لِوَجْهِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">for the sake of God;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to obtain the countenance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">favour,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">approbation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">recompense, of God</hi>]: (Msb:) or it means <hi rend="ital">in obedience to God;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">in the way of God</hi> or <hi rend="ital">his religion:</hi> (TA:) [or it may be rendered <hi rend="ital">for the sake of God Himself;</hi> and so <pb n="986"/> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لِوَجْهِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>: it is said to have been used by the Arabs [of the classical age], as well as by Aboo-Temmám, [who was a Muwelled;] (Mgh, Msb, *) but some deny that it occurs in the old language. (Msb. [See, however, an ex. from a trad. voce <foreign lang="ar">أُخَيْشِنُ</foreign>.]) [It is said that] the phrase <foreign lang="ar">مَجَلَّتُهُمْ ذَاتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الإِلٰهِ</foreign>, used by En-Nábighah, (Msb,) i. e. EdhDhubyánee, (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">جل</foreign>,) means <hi rend="ital">Their book is the service of God Himself:</hi> (Msb:) [but it seems more reasonable to render this phrase agreeably with the primary signification of <foreign lang="ar">ذات</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">their book is that of God,</hi> in a sense like that in which a house of worship is said to be a house of God; for,] as some relate it, the phrase used by En-Nábighah is <foreign lang="ar">مَحَلَّتُهُمْ ذَاتُ الإِلٰهِ</foreign>, with <foreign lang="ar">حاء</foreign>, [i. e. <hi rend="ital">their abode is</hi> in a peculiar manner <hi rend="ital">that of God,</hi>] meaning, their abode is one of pilgrimage and of sacred sites. (S and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">جل</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="15">-b15-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign> is sometimes redundant [in respect of meaning, though governing as a prefixed n.]; and so is its pl. See also what is said respecting <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign> prefixed to a proper name in an early portion of this paragraph.]          <sense type="b" n="16">-b16-</sense>  It is also used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">اَلَّذِى</foreign>, (T, S, M, K,) in the dial. of Teiyi, (T, S, TA,) for the purpose of qualifying a determinate noun (S, M, K) by means of a proposition which it connects with that noun: (M, K:) and when thus used, it [generally] retains the same form when it denotes a dual and a pl. (S, M, K) and a fem., (S,) and exhibits no sign of case: (M, K:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">أَنَا ذُو عَرَفْتُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I who knew</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">ذُو سَمِعْتُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">who heard</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">هٰذِهِ المَرْأَةُ ذُو قَالَتْ كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is the woman who said such a thing:</hi> (S:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَتَانِى ذُو</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَالَ ذٰلِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He who said that came to me</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">أَتَانِى ذُو قَالَا ذٰلِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They two who said that came to me</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">أَتَانِ ذُو قَالُوا ذٰلِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They who said that came to me</hi>]. (M.) But Fr says, I heard an Arab of the desert say, <foreign lang="ar">بِالفَضْلِ ذُو فَضَّلَكُمْ ٱللّٰهُ بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَالكَرَامَةِ ذَاتُ أَكْرَمَكُمُ ٱللّٰهُ بِهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">By the excellence wherewith God hath made you to excel, and the honour wherewith God hath honoured you</hi>]; thus they use <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتُ</foreign> in the place of <foreign lang="ar">اَلَّتِى</foreign>, and they make it to be with refa in every case: and they confuse [numbers and genders] in speaking of a dual number and a pl. number [and a fem.]; they sometimes say, [for ex.,] in the case of the dual, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَانِ ذُو تَعْرِفُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هَاتَانِ ذُو تَعْرِفُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">These two whom,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">which, thou knowest</hi>]; and a poet says, [namely, Sinán Ibn-El-Fahl, of the tribe of Teiyi, (Ham p. 292,)] <quote>

                        <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتُ يَنْهَضْنَ بِغَيْرِ سَائِقْ</foreign>

                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">I collected them from outstripping she-camels, that rise and hasten in their pace without a driver</hi>]; and the prov., <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى عَلَيْهِ ذُو أَتَى عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّاسِ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">الَّذِى أَتَى</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">What has come upon men</hi> in general <hi rend="ital">has come,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came, upon him</hi>]. (T.) Accord. to the usage most in repute, <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign> in this sense is indecl., and has no variation of gender or number; but some decline it, like <foreign lang="ar">ذو</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">صَاحِب</foreign>, except that they make <foreign lang="ar">ذَات</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَات</foreign> indecl., with damm for the termination, saying <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتُ</foreign> in every case, if they adopt the chaste mode; otherwise, in the accus. and gen. cases, saying <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتِ</foreign>, and in like manner <foreign lang="ar">ذَوَاتِ</foreign> (I' Ak pp. 40 and 41.)          <sense type="b" n="17">-b17-</sense>  They said also, <foreign lang="ar">لَاأَفْعَلُ ذٰلِكَ بِذِى تَسْلَمُ</foreign> (M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">بذى تَسْلَمِينَ</foreign>, (M,) and <foreign lang="ar">بذى تَسْلَمَانِ</foreign>, (M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">بذى تَسْلَمُونَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بذىتَسْلَمْنَ</foreign>, (M,) meaning <hi rend="ital">I will not do that by thy,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">by your, safety:</hi> (M, K:) or <hi rend="ital">by God who,</hi> (M,) or <hi rend="ital">by Him who,</hi> (K,) <hi rend="ital">maketh thee,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">you, to be in safety.</hi> (M, K.) [See also art. <foreign lang="ar">سلم</foreign>.]    </entryFree>25:T5ce,<entryFree id="n14143" key="ذَوَوِىٌّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ذَوَوِىٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> the rel. n. of <foreign lang="ar">ذُو</foreign>; (S, TA;) and of <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتٌ</foreign> also, (S, M, Msb, TA,) the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> of the original being rejected in forming the rel. n.: (S, Msb, * TA:)   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n14143-1" target="ذَاتِىٌّ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n13617"/></foreign>, as rel. n. of <foreign lang="ar">ذَاتٌ</foreign>, is not allowable: (M:) [but it is much used, mostly in philosophical and religious writings, as meaning <hi rend="ital">Essential,</hi> &amp;c.:] they say
